一_yī_one_A single horizontal stroke, representing the number one.__1_2
丁_dīng_cubes_In ancient scripts 丁 was written in two different ways: (1) depicting the walls of a city, which is now written as 圍, or (2) depicting a nail, which is now written as 釘.__2_1168
丂_kǎo_axe handle_Pictograph of an axe handle.__2_
七_qī_seven_Depicts two lines crossing. Based on the original meaning "cut", now written as 切. The current meaning is a phonetic loan.__2_530
丄_shàng_above_One stroke on top of another; variant of 上__2_
丅_xià_under___2_
丆_xx_kwukyel___2_
万_wàn,mò_ten thousand_Variant of 丏. Depicts a person (人) with a cover on top, conveying the original meaning "to not be seen". The current meaning is a phonetic loan. Simplified form of 萬._萬_3_322
丈_zhàng_unit of length ~ 3 meters_Depicts 10 (十) hand-lengths (又): 丈 (~3 meters) is a traditional Chinese unit of length equal to 10 尺 (~0.3 meters). The current use of 丈 as "husband" is a phonetic loan.__3_1242
三_sān_three_Three horizontal strokes, representing the number three.__3_125
上_shàng,shǎng_up_Originally a small line or dot above a longer line, indicating "up". The vertical line was added to distinguish the character from 二 (two). Opposite of 下.__3_16
下_xià_under_Originally a small line or dot below a longer line, indicating "down". The vertical line was added to distinguish the character from 二 (two). Opposite of 上.__3_42
丌_jī,qí_table_Depicts a table.__3_
不_bù_no_Pictograph of sepals of a flower. The modern meaning "no" is a phonetic loan.__4_4
与_yǔ,yù,yú_and_Simplified form of 與.  Phonosemantic compound. 舁 represents the meaning and 牙 represents the sound.  The traditional component 舁 was removed for simplification._與_3_108
丏_miǎn_parapet_Depicts a person (人) with a cover on top, conveying the original meaning "to not be seen". The meaning later shifted to "invisible" and "parapet".__4_
丐_gài_beggar_Depicts the blade of a knife. Similar in origin to 亡 and 方. Based on the original meaning "cut". The current meaning is a phonetic loan._匃,匄_4_2606
丑_chǒu_second earthly branch; (simp.) ugly_Depicts of a hand or paw with fingernails or claws. The current meaning is a phonetic loan. In simplified Chinese 丑 is also used to mean "ugly", while in traditional Chinese this meaning is written with a separate character 醜._醜_4_1901
丒_chǒu_the period from 1 to 3 a.m.___4_
专_zhuān_monopolize_Depicts a hand (寸) spinning a wheel (叀). Based on the original meaning "turn", now written as 轉. The current meaning is a phonetic loan. The simplified character 专 was adapted from the cursive form of the traditional character 專._專,耑_4_485
且_qiě_moreover_Originally a pictograph of a sacrificial altar. The current meaning "moreover" is a phonetic loan.__5_296
丕_pī_great___5_3748
世_shì_generation_Origin unclear. Various explanations include (1) depicting three leaves on branches of a tree, a remnant from the top part of 枼 (leaf), which was phonetically similar in Old Chinese, (2) three dots added above the phonetically similar 止 (zhǐ - foot), or (3) three copies of 十 (ten), similar to the archaic character 卅 (thirty), depicting a 30-year generation.__5_181
丗_shì_thirty___5_
丘_qiū_hill_Pictograph of two hills._坵_5_1929
丙_bǐng_third_Depicts a platform to put things on. The current meaning is a phonetic loan.__5_2645
业_yè_profession_Simplified character from the top 5 strokes of the traditional 業. Depicts a person (大) carrying a weapon (丵). Based on the original meaning "attack". The meaning later shifted to "expand territory" and "develop business"._業_5_130
丛_cóng_bush_Simplified form of 叢. 从 represents the sound._叢_5_1678
东_dōng_east_Pictograph of a basket or a bag. The current meaning "east" is a phonetic loan. The simplified character 东 was adapted from the cursive form of the traditional character 東._東_5_194
丝_sī_silk, threads_Simplified form of 絲.  Duplication of 纟 (silk)._絲_5_1026
丞_chéng_assist_Depicts two hands (廾) rescuing a person (卩) trapped in a pit (凵).__6_3340
丟_diū_lose, discard_A horizontal line, depicting an item being discarded, added to the semantically similar character 去 (leave; go).__6_1639
丠_qiū_hill___6_
両_liǎng_two___6_
丢_diū_lose, discard_A horizontal line, depicting an item being discarded, added to the semantically similar character 去 (leave; go)._丟_6_1639
丣_yǒu_ancient form of the tenth of the twelve Terrestrial Branches___7_
两_liǎng_two_Simplified form of 兩.  Combination of two 丙 characters. 丙 also represents the sound._兩_7_133
严_yán_strict_Simplified form of 嚴.  Phonosemantic compound. 喦 represents the meaning and 敢 represents the sound. Based on the original meaning "exaggerate". The meaning later shifted to "extreme", "severe", and "strict". The traditional component 敢 was removed for simplification._嚴_7_545
並_bìng_side by side_Depits two people standing (立) side by side.__8_141
丧_sàng,sāng_mourning_Simplified form of 喪. Depicts multiple mouths (口) wailing to mourn the death (亡). 桑 and 亡 represent the sound._喪_8_1404
丨_gǔn,shù_vertical line___1_
丩_jiū_join_Pictograph of two ropes entangled together, now written as 糾.__2_
个_gè,gě_[measure word]_Pictograph of one stalk of bamboo. Same as one half of the character for bamboo (竹)._個,箇_3_12
丫_yā_forked_Pictograph of a fork or branch.__3_2682
丬_qiáng_piece of wood_丬 is a component form of 爿._爿_3_
中_zhōng,zhòng_central_Depicts a flagpole. There is a circle in the middle marking the center of the flagpole. In older forms of the character, the flagpole  has streamers at the top and bottom used to show the direction of the wind__4_14
丮_jǐ_catch_Pictograph of a person with both hands outstretched.__4_
丰_fēng_luxuriant_Depicts a growing plant with leaves._豐_4_1189
丱_guàn,kuàng_child's hairstyle bound in two tufts_Pictograph of a child's hairstyle with two tufts.__5_
串_chuàn_string_Pictograph of two objects on a skewer or strung together.__7_1832

临_lín_draw near_Simplified form of 臨.  Depicts a person (人) looking (臣) down at a pile of objects (品). 品 also represents the sound. Based on the original meaning, "to look down". The meaning has shifted over time and now means "draw near"._臨_9_839

事_shì_matter_The characters 史 (history), 吏 (government official), 使 (cause; use; instruct), and 事 (matter; work; affair) are all etymologically related and all derive from the same ancient character, depicting a hand (又) holding a container for writing utensils. 事 and 史 were originally written the same, but later an extra mark was added to distinguish them.__8_58

周_zhōu_cycle_Originally depicted farmland. The meaning later shifted to "circumference" and "cycle". Later the 口 component was added when 周 was used to refer to a geographical region to indicate that the character was only "mouthed", i.e. used for its sound. In simplified Chinese 周 is also used to mean "week", while in traditional Chinese this meaning is written with a separate character 週._週_8_490

癸_guǐ_10th heavenly stem_Origin unclear. Various explanations include (1) a pictograph of a type of ancient weapon, which could be the original form of 戣, (2) pictograph of four leaves growing opposite from each other or the head of a sunflower, which could be the original form of 葵, or (3) pictograph of two arrows intersecting each other. Either way, the original form is unrelated to the current meaning.__9_4414
